{"kind": "blogger#postList", "nextPageToken": "CgkIChiAtuzhsCYQy4Ca9ZL8nrwx", "items": [{"kind": "blogger#post", "id": "4605692687665217525", "blog": {"id": "3564735312144269387"}, "published": "2011-11-02T06:56:00+05:30", "updated": "2013-08-16T19:31:24+05:30", "etag": "\"iHf3yWDE_geBgZ8U7rgZ_xuTeAQ/dGltZXN0YW1wOiAxMzc2NjYxNjg0Njk2Cm9mZnNldDogMTk4MDAwMDAK\"", "url": "http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2011/11/vaikom-muhammad-basheer-sultan-of-story.html", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/4605692687665217525", "title": "VAIKOM MUHAMMAD BASHEER, THE SULTAN OF STORY TELLERS-  CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL", "content": "<div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"text-align: left;\" trbidi=\"on\">\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Z1PQOLZYN08/TrCb6eMKTiI/AAAAAAAAHoI/2LxpD0yFbS4/s1600/imagesCAJV8W29.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Z1PQOLZYN08/TrCb6eMKTiI/AAAAAAAAHoI/2LxpD0yFbS4/s1600/imagesCAJV8W29.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Vaikom Muhammad Basheer was a fiction writer, who wrote in my mother tongue Malayalam. He passed away at the age of 86 from my hometown Calicut, in 1994, leaving behind his wife and two children.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">He won the Padma Shri award in 1992. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>His face adorns one of the Govt of India postal stamps.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">People outside Kerala will surely ask Vaikom Mohammad Basheer , who?<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Well this was a man who broke all shackles of contemporary Malayalam literature. He did not care for the classical language\u2014 rather he did NOT even know it. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>He wrote in Kozhikkodan Mappila Malayalam, the colloquial vernacular of the Kerala Muslims, or rather he wrote in the language of his characters.&nbsp;<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Every Malayali film goer knows the delightful vernacular used by character artist and comedian Mammu Koya. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">I relate to this style . When I was a kid I used to come rushing back home from<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>school , to play with my neighbouring kids,<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>some of <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>whom were Muslims , who spoke this Malayalam strain slang. There were about 16 of us playing soccer and Chatti ( 7 tiles ) . Those were happy childhood days.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The writings of Basheer are like a whiff of fresh air , after the first rain on parched land. Once you start reading his simple but well crafted stories , you won\u2019t stop till you finish it. And after you reach the end of the story, you will be silent for a while and ponder over what he wrote\u2014literally the melody of a song which lingers.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Malayalam literature till then, was monopolized by the high caste Hindus who wrote boring stuff in Sanskritised Malayam , which went over the heads of the common man. Trying to impress with prose rather than content, was never Basheer\u2019s forte. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>Basheer\u2019s style in contract was refreshingly down to earth and rustic. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>You really cannot translate his stories into other languages without knocking out its punch and sheen.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">He was an astute observer of human nature, and the darker and seamier side of poverty. Every story had a social commitment and theme, woven craftily into the plot sometimes as sarcasm or even black humor. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The Malayali women just loved to shed a silent tear over his mushy love stories. His stories were poignant, full of emotional intensity,<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>mostly in a lingering sad way, which gave you a lump in your throat. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>He also could punch humour in between, in a unique style which appealed to all age groups and intelligence levels. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Literally Basheer , with his deep understanding of raw human emotions exploded the Malayali consciousness to a new level, all by simple earthy stories. His magic with words made the Malayalis laugh, then he made them cry, before they could stop laughing. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>If Basheer\u2019s stories were the North pole the hollow Yank TV serial, \u201c The bold and the beautiful\u201d would be the south pole. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>Basheer\u2019s inimitable works<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>were thankfully free of pomp and ostentation.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Now how did he get to understand raw human emotions?<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Mostly by self experience , where he faced death due to hunger several times.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Experience is verily the best master. His personal life had been a sort of \u201cPapillon\u201d type saga. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>The sheer trauma and gory reality of life that Basheer roller coasted through in his young eventful life did not allow him to lead a sane and peaceful life-- he was twice admitted to mental sanatoriums.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In 1924, when Mahatma Gandhi came to his village Vaikom for the Vaikom Satyagraha, 16 year old Basheer wore Khadi and went to meet him. He got thrashed by his headmaster for wearing Khadee.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>He jostled his way to Gandhiji\u2019s car . He came back and told his mother proudly \u201cUmma, I managed to touch Gandhiji\u2019s hand today!\u201d\u2014probably the turning point of his life.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In 1930 he participated in Gandhiji\u2019s Salt satyagraha at Malabar, and was thrown into Kannur prison for 3 months. In 1931 he was editor of a revolutionary magazine by the name of Ujjvanam ( Uprising ), and a warrant was issued for his arrest again. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">He fled Kerala to evade arrest and was footloose for 7 years. He went all around India in various disguises. He stayed in hermitages in Himalayas with Hindu sages.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>He even stowed away on a Merchant ship SS Rizwani along with Mecca pilgrims ,&nbsp;and went abroad to Gulf . To keep himself alive he took on various jobs cook,<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>fruit juice seller, beggar, newspaper boy, accountant, shepherd, watchman, hotel boy, porter, <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>fortune teller ( crafty guy giving bull !) , errand boy etc. He says he lost his hair due to lack of nutrition.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Cpa6P7mYI2A/TrCb_BvIs8I/AAAAAAAAHoQ/QIB6EFc-CvA/s1600/bbb.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Cpa6P7mYI2A/TrCb_BvIs8I/AAAAAAAAHoQ/QIB6EFc-CvA/s1600/bbb.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">All these experiences , while struggling to keep himself alive and staving off hunger, were the reason for his deep understanding of human character and nature. After he returned back to Kerala he again plunged headlong into the freedom struggle and went to couple of <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>times more. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">He wrote about his own experiences in jail too. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>One of them \u201cMathilugal\u201d was made into a Malayalam movie starring super star Mammotty, directed by renowned director Adoor Gopalakrishnan.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathilukal\" title=\"Mathilukal\"><i><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"color: windowtext; font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-fareast-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\">Mathilukal</span></i></a><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-fareast-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\"> (\"Walls\") is Basheer\u2019s own story . It is a novel of sad irony set against a turbulent pre-independence days political backdrop.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Here prisoner Basheer<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>falls in love with a 22 year old life convict Hindu woman . The women\u2019s jail was separated from men\u2019s jail by a very high wall. One day he was trying to catch a squirrel. Suddenly a woman's voice from beyond the compound wall asked: <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>'Who is whistling over there?\" Till that moment of time , Basheer was resigned to mechanically living out each day in the prison till his sentence gets over. He gets renewed hope and energy in his monotonous life in the prison, when he starts interacting daily with this sweet female voice from across the walls, from the women\u2019s prison. They fall passionately in love, exchange tokens of love across the wall, device a code to signal when they want to listen to each others\u2019 voices, and so on. There are priceless steaming conversations between them from both sides of the wall. He now has a reason to wake up to each day, to look forward to hearing Narayani\u2019s voice, and to replay each of their words a hundred times before he drifts off to sleep dreaming of her in his arms . They strategize on how to catch a glimpse of each other\u2026They exchange solemn love-promises standing on two sides of a wall, only to be separated , one fine day without even being able to say good-bye. On the day they planned to meet at the prison hospital, by a strange quirk of fate, Basheer was released. He never had a chance to tell her . <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>Before he \"met\" Naraayani, the prison walls were killing Basheer, but when the orders for his release arrive he falls apart and loudly protests, \"Who needs freedom? Outside these walls lies an even bigger jail.\"</span><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-TzupN46-1fw/TrH4eK3-mAI/AAAAAAAAHsY/wR5tDY_Jveo/s1600/imagesCAEFX3WV.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"257\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-TzupN46-1fw/TrH4eK3-mAI/AAAAAAAAHsY/wR5tDY_Jveo/s320/imagesCAEFX3WV.jpg\" width=\"320\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-fareast-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;\">For breathing life into this role, Mammotty got Best Actor National award.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-aPvl4aL0rWk/TrCcDc7m1TI/AAAAAAAAHoY/M23FkZONsjA/s1600/NNN.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-aPvl4aL0rWk/TrCcDc7m1TI/AAAAAAAAHoY/M23FkZONsjA/s1600/NNN.gif\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<div style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<strong>Published Works</strong><o:p></o:p></div>\n<br />\n<div style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-left: 0.25in;\">\n<i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\">1. Premalekhanam [ A love letter] (Novel) (1943).<br />\n2. Baalyakaalasakhi [ Sweetheart from childhood] (Novel) (1944).<br />\n3. Kathaabeejam [ Seed of a story ] (Play) (1945).<br />\n4. Janmadinam [Birthday] (Short stories) (1945).<br />\n5. Ormakkurippu [Jottings from memory] (Short stories) (1946).<br />\n6. Anargha nimisham [Invaluable instant] (See Anal Haq) (Short stories) (1946).<br />\n7. Shabdangal [Voices] (Novel) (1947).<br />\n8. Viddhikalude Swargam [Fools' paradise] (Short stories) (1948).<br />\n9. Ente uppuppakkoru aana undayirunnu [Me grandad had an elephant] (Novel) (1951).<br />\n10. Maranathininde Nizhalil [In the shadow of death] (Novel) (1951).<br />\n11. Muchcheettu kalikkaarande Makal [The daughter of the card-shark] (Novel) (1951).<br />\n12. Paavappettavarudey Vaeshya [The courtesan of the poor] (Short stories) (1952).<br />\n13. Sthalathe Pradhaana Divyan [The principal divine of the place] (Novel) (1953).<br />\n14. Aanavaariyum Ponkurishum [Elephant rustler and Golden cross] (Novel) (1953).<br />\n15. Jeevithanizhalppaadukal [The shadows of life] (Novel) (1954).<br />\n16. Vishwavikhkhyaathamaaya Mookku [The world-renowned nose] (Short stories) (1954).<br />\n17. Vishappu [Hunger] (Short stories) (1954).<br />\n18. Paaththummayude Aadu [Paaththumma's goat] (Novel) (1959).<br />\n19. Mathilukal [Walls] (Novel; basis for a film (1989) by Adoor Gopalakrishnan) (1965).<br />\n20. Oru Bhagavadgeethayum Kuraey Mulakalum [A Bhagavadgeetha and some breasts] (Short stories) (1967).<br />\n21. Thaaraa Specials (Novel) (1968).<br />\n22. Maanthrika poochcha [The magic cat] (Novel) (1968).<br />\n23. Nerum Nunayum [Truth and lie] (Commentary and letters) (1969).<br />\n24. Ormmayudaey Arakal [The cells of memory] (Commentary and reminiscences) (1973).<br />\n25. Aanappooda [Elephant-hair] (Short stories) (1975).<br />\n26. Chirikkunna Marappaava [The laughing wooden doll] (Short stories) (1975).<br />\n27. Bhoomiyudaey Avakaashikal [The inheritors of the earth] (Short stories) (1977).<br />\n28. Anuraagaththintaey Dhinangal [The days of desire] (Diary; originally titled Kaamukantaey diary [The diary of the paramour] and changed later on the suggestion of M. T. Vasudevan Nair) (1983).<br />\n29. Bhaargavinilayam [The house named Bhaargavi] (Screenplay for a film (1964) by A. Vincent which is credited as the first horror cinema in malayalam; adapted from the short story Neelavelichcham [The blue glow]) (1985).<br />\n30. M. P. Paul (Reminiscences of his friendship with M. P. Paul) (1991).<br />\n31. Shinkidimunkan (Short stories) (1991).<br />\n32. Cheviyorkkuka! Anthimakaahalam!! [Hark! The final clarion-call!!] (Speech) (1992).<br />\n33. Yaa Ilaahi! [Oh God!] (Short stories published posthumously) (1997).<o:p></o:p></i></div>\n<br />\n<div style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\nWhen he achieved fame some Islamic fundamentalist organisations tried to make Basheer their mouthpiece, to highlight their cause .<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>To Basheer\u2019s credit he did NOT fall prey to them, earning the respect of all. <o:p></o:p></div>\n<br />\n<div style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\nYou may wonder\u2014what the hell? <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>Everybody writes a love story. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>The usual run of the mill, man meets girl\u2014 man falls in love \u2014 <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>man proposes to girl \u2014 <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>girls ignores him \u2014 <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>man does sweet pursuit\u2014 <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>girl relents after playing hard to get for a respectable period . <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span><o:p></o:p></div>\n<br />\n<div style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\nThousands of love stories had the same plot, right? <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>So then why is Basheer so special?<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Well, ladies and gentlemen, <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>that is why Basheer is the sultan of all legendary story tellers.<o:p></o:p></div>\n<br />\n<div style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\">By the way Aishwarya Rai calls sweet pursuit of love -- <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>\u201c diabolical stalking\u201d. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span><span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>Poor girl, at the age of 38 is still hooked on to the \u201cCoz I am worth it\u201d <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>line \u2013<o:p></o:p></i></div>\n<br />\n<div style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\">No easy escape from narcissm for some \u2013 Basheer on the contrary was unaffected all all the attention\u2014anybody muse could go to his doorstep and interrupt his writing. Did not a little bird tweet , that beauty is only skin deep?<o:p></o:p></i></div>\n<br />\n<div style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\">\u201c LoReal Paris, ka Total Repair 5-- Kyon ki mujhe naaz hai khud par\u201d! ( sniff !) . I wonder how Basheer would have responded to this pathetic line!!</i><br />\n<br />\nBasheer should have written a book about Kerala Communists-- how they keep dropping the Latin word <span style=\"color: red; font-size: x-large;\">BOURGEOIS</span> without knowing its meaning , all over the place&nbsp;to impress all and sundry.&nbsp; The best part is , surprisingly&nbsp;-- all of them know how to pronounce this word properly.&nbsp; I remember the Calicut Communist Muncipal Corporation used to make problems for us at the Stadium Tennis clay court -- dubbing it&nbsp;a bourgeois ( sic!) game.<br />\n<br />\n<span style=\"color: blue;\">In the video below the delightful , hilarious dialogues of Mammu Koya who speaks the Mappila lingo of Basheer, can never ever be recreated in any other language. </span><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<object class=\"BLOGGER-youtube-video\" classid=\"clsid:D27CDB6E-AE6D-11cf-96B8-444553540000\" codebase=\"http://download.macromedia.com/pub/shockwave/cabs/flash/swflash.cab#version=6,0,40,0\" data-thumbnail-src=\"http://3.gvt0.com/vi/ggI__8_lw7c/0.jpg\" height=\"266\" width=\"320\"><param name=\"movie\" value=\"http://www.youtube.com/v/ggI__8_lw7c&fs=1&source=uds\" /><param name=\"bgcolor\" value=\"#FFFFFF\" /><embed width=\"320\" height=\"266\"  src=\"http://www.youtube.com/v/ggI__8_lw7c&fs=1&source=uds\" type=\"application/x-shockwave-flash\"></embed></object></div>\n<br />\nGrace and peace !<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Jtz90p-c97s/TrCbyhfToiI/AAAAAAAAHoA/5vUU9Mbk4wQ/s1600/21102011505.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"267\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Jtz90p-c97s/TrCbyhfToiI/AAAAAAAAHoA/5vUU9Mbk4wQ/s320/21102011505.jpg\" width=\"320\" /></a></div>\n<div style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; He made up by sheer left foot canon shot power, amazing ball control&nbsp;and&nbsp;&nbsp;supreme footballing intelligence.on the field.&nbsp; <br />\n<br />\nNobody could steal the ball from this tiny powerhouse. <br />\n<br />\nHe was the purest striker the world would ever see.<br />\n<br />\nPuskas could anticipate, he was a magician. Today I wonder, if Puskas had 1/4th fitness of Cristiano Ronaldo, what he would have been.<br />\n<br />\nHis left foot was a thunderbolt, and he terrorised goalkeepers from 35 metres away. Those days the leather ball was very heavy and would not play ball to &nbsp;\"bend it like Beckham \" modern day shots.<br />\n<br />\nPuskas was my childhood hero. Often I would read his soccer comic strips ( Hotspur, Hornet, Boy's world, Sportweek ) and day dream .<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-KbxeUdW2-MU/TqZGIYLSz9I/AAAAAAAAHTg/vs5Rf3kXdBw/s1600/bbb.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-KbxeUdW2-MU/TqZGIYLSz9I/AAAAAAAAHTg/vs5Rf3kXdBw/s1600/bbb.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\nStarting from the tender age of 18, he scored 84 goals in 85 international matches, till he retired at the age of 39 in 1966. His career tally stands at 1176 goals . Pele&nbsp;does NOT even come close, as second best.<br />\n<br />\n<br />\nPuskas had scored 157 goals in 182 games for Real Madrid. They have NOT forgotten this giant among giants on the soccer field, who gave them 5 La Liga championships in a row.&nbsp; After his death in 2006, at the age of 79, they gave him a pre-game RIP tribute. <br />\n<br />\nSee video below.<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<object class=\"BLOGGER-youtube-video\" classid=\"clsid:D27CDB6E-AE6D-11cf-96B8-444553540000\" codebase=\"http://download.macromedia.com/pub/shockwave/cabs/flash/swflash.cab#version=6,0,40,0\" data-thumbnail-src=\"http://0.gvt0.com/vi/9oEt4zQZ9Jg/0.jpg\" height=\"266\" width=\"320\"><param name=\"movie\" value=\"http://www.youtube.com/v/9oEt4zQZ9Jg&fs=1&source=uds\" />\n<param name=\"bgcolor\" value=\"#FFFFFF\" />\n<embed width=\"320\" height=\"266\"  src=\"http://www.youtube.com/v/9oEt4zQZ9Jg&fs=1&source=uds\" type=\"application/x-shockwave-flash\"></embed></object></div>\n<br />\n<br />\nPuskas and his Real Madrid partner&nbsp;Argentinian Alfredo De Stefano as partner, was the&nbsp; most feared finishing duo in international soccer.<br />\n<br />\nPuskas was the core of the Hungarian team which went unbeaten for a world record 32 games, during which they became Olympic Champions in 1952.<br />\n<br />\nNo wonder for the 1954 World Cup , Hungary flew in as top contenders. Puskas played the first two matches. In the first game&nbsp;Hungary clinically demolished South Korea 9-0 . <br />\n<br />\nConspiracies were soon hatched by the West. How dare a communist team , take the limelight in this manner. <br />\n<br />\nIn the second game against&nbsp;West Germany , Puskas was marked by Greman butcher Werner Liebrich&nbsp; who felled him repeatedly and mercilessly, with the western referee looking the other way. <br />\n<br />\nPuskas got a hairline fracture on his ankle and retired , still Hungary won easily 8-3.&nbsp; Puskas with 3 goals in his kitty, &nbsp;was ruled out of the World cup and he risked his footballing career if he played with a painful hairline fracture.<br />\n<br />\nIn the next game the Brazilians being poor losers invaded the Hungarian dressing room after the match and attacked them.&nbsp; In the free for all Brazilian coach Zeze Moreira punched and slapped the Hungarian sports minister.<br />\n<br />\n<br />\nIn the semi-finals ,without Puskas, &nbsp;Hungary struggled against Uruguay,&nbsp;had to play an epic 120 minutes and were exhausted --they won 4-2. <br />\n<br />\nThe 1954 World Cup finals was at Wankdorf stadium Berne against West Germany, whom they had slaughtered 8-3 before. <br />\n<br />\nThe playground was deliberately made slushy by excessive watering, which suited the Germans playing with special Adidas shoes, while Hungarians had communist soccer boots without cleats. <br />\n<br />\n60000 people crammed into the stadium , to watch the \"magical Magyars\" who had NOT lost in 4 years.<br />\n<br />\nIt is now understood, after extensive study of footage&nbsp;by University of Leipzig that the Germans were injected with steroid drugs Methamphitamine , before the match and also orally during the half break, making them indefatigable. The German players were told it was Vitamin C injection, and those days there were no drug tests..<br />\n<br />\nPuskas declared himself fit, a huge sacrifice though he was limping. Within 6 minutes of the start of the game, Puskas scored.&nbsp; Two minutes later Hungarian forward Czibor scored again. <br />\n<br />\nAfter that what happened is still a mystery to the whole world. <br />\n<br />\nToday people say that some Hungarian players were bribed. In the rain, hard and rough playing Germany clawed back and scored thrice.&nbsp; <br />\n<br />\nJust before the end of the game Puskas scored a beauty, past goalkeeper Terek , but this goal was disallowed by the British referee William Ling, supported by the&nbsp;Welsh&nbsp;linesman Mervyn Griffiths.&nbsp; <br />\n<br />\nEverybody were stunned as the goal was clearly legitimate. <br />\n<br />\nIt was obvious that even God could not make COMMUNIST Hungary win that day, -- it was all fixed.<br />\n<br />\nTHE 1954 WORLD CUP ISTODAY KNOWN IN SPORTS QUIZ PROGRAMMES AS THE&nbsp;\"CUP WHICH HUNGARY LOST\"<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<object class=\"BLOGGER-youtube-video\" classid=\"clsid:D27CDB6E-AE6D-11cf-96B8-444553540000\" codebase=\"http://download.macromedia.com/pub/shockwave/cabs/flash/swflash.cab#version=6,0,40,0\" data-thumbnail-src=\"http://0.gvt0.com/vi/U9z5Fghf22Q/0.jpg\" height=\"266\" width=\"320\"><param name=\"movie\" value=\"http://www.youtube.com/v/U9z5Fghf22Q&fs=1&source=uds\" />\n<param name=\"bgcolor\" value=\"#FFFFFF\" />\n<embed width=\"320\" height=\"266\"  src=\"http://www.youtube.com/v/U9z5Fghf22Q&fs=1&source=uds\" type=\"application/x-shockwave-flash\"></embed></object></div>\n<br />\n<br />\nIn a career spanning 23 years Puskas won 3 European cups, 10 national championships, and 8 top individual top scorer awards. <br />\n<br />\nHe is remembered for his grace, great heart and jovial nature, unlike the cold and snooty players, &nbsp;like Cristiano Ronaldo nowadays.<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-eFngVRh8q78/TqZFmlKrChI/AAAAAAAAHTQ/Pj2UV7vqp14/s1600/imagesvvv.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-eFngVRh8q78/TqZFmlKrChI/AAAAAAAAHTQ/Pj2UV7vqp14/s1600/imagesvvv.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\nProbably being from a communist country, and that too a Major in the army cost him a place in the glorious annals of football. In Oct 2009, FIFA made late amends by introducing FIFA Puskas award for the \"most beautiful goal\".<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-AcZwCuh-b6w/TqZFc_Emr5I/AAAAAAAAHTA/fgZ1tjQFRxc/s1600/ppp.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; Pele is far behind, almost lack lustre.&nbsp; <br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-LbfQRaKIpBA/TqZFg_1ExVI/AAAAAAAAHTI/DdMkfFUPmDQ/s1600/imagesppp.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em;
